        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3193144848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15415661383763385561">Well first, the fact that this book was written within 5-6 weeks is impressive. I was amazed from John le Carr√©'s afterword that this book was not only written during that short span but also under a lot of work related and personal stress. This was a slow burn kind of spy novel with the British agent Alec Leamas who is given an assignment to infiltrate East German Intelligence and bring down its leading man. Well the setting is during the cold war, the book itself was published in 1963. The wor</span>
  <span id="freeText15415661383763385561" style="display:none">Well first, the fact that this book was written within 5-6 weeks is impressive. I was amazed from John le Carr√©'s afterword that this book was not only written during that short span but also under a lot of work related and personal stress. This was a slow burn kind of spy novel with the British agent Alec Leamas who is given an assignment to infiltrate East German Intelligence and bring down its leading man. Well the setting is during the cold war, the book itself was published in 1963. The world has changed much since socio-politically while still remaining the same in certain ways. The fear of a world nuclear obliteration has declined, but I think the fear, curiosity and general hysteria from that era must have helped the success of this book. <br /><br />The book is written in economical yet descriptive prose that captures skillfully the atmosphere of skepticism, fear, cunning and despair. As I was reading I was amazed at what I felt was an accurate description of British intelligence systems or intelligence systems in general, not because I've ever been involved with any intelligence/surveillance agency of any kind but simply because of the certainty and command in the writing, only for me to discover later that John le Carr√© was a British spy in the 50s and 60s like Alec. I think certain things that would have made this a more pleasurable read have been diluted by the numerous spy films I've watched, much of the book was read with confirmed expectancy with the exception of that incredible final twist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15415661383763385561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/93114967-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781611760927" href="/book/show/13589086-the-spy-who-came-in-from-the-cold">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93114967-barbara?shelf=spy-thriller">spy-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93114967-barbara?shelf=smiley">smiley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3224038596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7742815853347525818">The third of the Smiley books, which I'm reading in order this year. <br/><br/>What a giant step forward from the first two books! It's easy to see why it was a best seller. Here we first see the full blossoming of disillusionment with the Cold War that permeates so much of le Carr√©'s writing from this point on. The layers of duplicity, the use of individuals as pawns in international politics, the exploration of whether it's possible for either side to be truly honorable - they are all here.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19494.The_Spy_Who_Came_In_from_the_Cold' title='The Spy Who Came In from the Cold by John le Carr√©' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Spy Who C</a></span>
  <span id="freeText7742815853347525818" style="display:none">The third of the Smiley books, which I'm reading in order this year. <br /><br />What a giant step forward from the first two books! It's easy to see why it was a best seller. Here we first see the full blossoming of disillusionment with the Cold War that permeates so much of le Carr√©'s writing from this point on. The layers of duplicity, the use of individuals as pawns in international politics, the exploration of whether it's possible for either side to be truly honorable - they are all here.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19494.The_Spy_Who_Came_In_from_the_Cold" title="The Spy Who Came In from the Cold by John le Carr√©" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spy Who Came In from the Cold</a> is also so much more fully and capably written than the first two books. It's a mature handling of the tone le Carr√© was working toward previously. No false notes here. Although I was already familiar with the book and knew the conclusion, I still found myself tensely gripping the wheel of my own car as I drove down the road during the final pages. A first rate job of creating and releasing tension throughout the entire book.<br /><br />Smiley is much more in the background here than in the previous books, although his presence can always be felt through the events he sets in motion. <br /><br />I'm truly enjoying this sequential re-read project. Can't wait for the next volume, though I plan to hold off a while, savoring this one just a bit longer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7742815853347525818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2231715-lewis-weinstein?shelf=crime-and-thrillers">crime-and-thrillers</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64770243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15508457281242344272">I have now finished my re-read, and I'm not sure if I'm happy or not that I didn't remember the ending. It's a thrilling story.<br/><br/>The way the story is presented ... what is revealed, what is held back, and the sequence of revelation ... is so superb. Any writer can benefit by outlining the scenes.<br/><br/>And of course there are the flawed characters, brilliant and stupid, compassionate and cold-hearted, none of them to be trusted, who populate all of le Carre's work.</span>

          </span>

Coward-Mccann, Inc. published the first American edition of the novel in New York in 1964.<br/><br/>Set during the political tensions of the Cold War, the revolutionary espionage novel portrays the intelligence services of both Eastern and Western nations as sacrificing morality in the name of national security. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422914107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1073937813406083121">Okay, I'm fully ready to dive into a non-stop Le Carr√© bender! <br/><br/>These are great spy novels. And these are quality books, period. The man can write. Plus, his experiences in intelligence work paid off HUGE. The intricacies of spy networks and secret government agencies are spread over these pages like caviar and go down like a perfectly aged wine. Shit damn, this is sweet stuff!<br/><br/>Now, before you get all amped up, John le Carr√© does not write James Bond stuff. There are no car chases and inventive ga</span>
  <span id="freeText1073937813406083121" style="display:none">Okay, I'm fully ready to dive into a non-stop Le Carr√© bender! <br /><br />These are great spy novels. And these are quality books, period. The man can write. Plus, his experiences in intelligence work paid off HUGE. The intricacies of spy networks and secret government agencies are spread over these pages like caviar and go down like a perfectly aged wine. Shit damn, this is sweet stuff!<br /><br />Now, before you get all amped up, John le Carr√© does not write James Bond stuff. There are no car chases and inventive gadgetry. No femme fatales succumb to his heroes. Sure, love is involved, but it's generally more realistic. It's all more realistic, when it comes down to it.<br /><br />In <i>The Spy Who Came In from the Cold</i> a pissed off agent, who lost his network of spies to a crafty and conniving bastard of a super agent, is sent out into the field again as a plant to ferret out the bad guy. The agent is a pawn without knowledge of the whole affair and he knows it. But hell, he's willing to do anything to get revenge. This emotional attachment to the job puts him at yet another disadvantage. But he's good, so he should be able to handle himself...right?<br /><br />Read and find out! Another highly recommended novel from John le Carr√©!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_165164624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165164624" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335664-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551667298p2/3335664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165164624?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3335664-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781602836587" href="/book/show/6618344-the-spy-who-came-in-from-the-cold">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Burned-out spies</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=modern-classic">modern-classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=germany">germany</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=1960s">1960s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=spy">spy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=1001-books-to-read-before-you-die">1001-books-to-read-before-you-die</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165164624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1869434052659982766">Having just indulged my sweet tooth with Ian Fleming's spy candy, I sampled the more refined pleasures of John le Carr√©, who wrote a tense spy thriller without any gadgets or heroics or sultry seductresses. Instead, Alec Leamas is a middle-aged alcoholic on the verge of retirement from the spy game; burned out, embittered, and about to be cashiered for a string of failures while running England's spy network in Cold War Berlin. He's recruited for one final mission: to target the dangerous East G</span>
  <span id="freeText1869434052659982766" style="display:none">Having just indulged my sweet tooth with Ian Fleming's spy candy, I sampled the more refined pleasures of John le Carr√©, who wrote a tense spy thriller without any gadgets or heroics or sultry seductresses. Instead, Alec Leamas is a middle-aged alcoholic on the verge of retirement from the spy game; burned out, embittered, and about to be cashiered for a string of failures while running England's spy network in Cold War Berlin. He's recruited for one final mission: to target the dangerous East German spymaster who's been responsible for the deaths of so many Western agents. His mission is almost derailed when he falls in love with a naive librarian who also happens to be a member of the Communist Party in England. There's some action and danger, but only in a few quick, confusing encounters in the dark. And there are tons of twists and double-crosses; everything works out logically in the end, but along the way le Carr√© jerks you around making you think first one person, then the other is the traitor, the double-agent, the one who's really been pulling the strings all along. The ending is a bitter and amoral one as Leamas discovers what he already knew, that there may be good guys and bad guys in the Cold War, but everyone is gray in the dark.<br /><br />This was a <i>great</i> spy story. Read Fleming for fun, but read le Carr√© for a more literary thriller where spies actually act like spies, and believable human beings, and everyone is a little bit dirty. Le Carr√© writes without a lot of excess description, but the dialog brings the characters to life, and it's the plot where he excels. There are no gratuitous scenes catering to the men's magazine readership (like with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164686401" rel="nofollow noopener">naked gypsy catfights</a>) and a lot less of the racist, sexist pandering; this is a much more intellectual story. The climax is a showdown between rival secret agents but not on a speeding train but in an East German secret trial where control over the outcome bounces back and forth like a ping-pong ball, carried entirely by characters delivering monologues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1869434052659982766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iLqS2sAQaljD3sxTWJ5+8ETRSEmXOTm9E1GThcBLxbqynPsIe06jMGT1eDKva3Qvko6vgVm0t9pIL9U0DQg3IA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m1CDBbe3C22AjlOhz3vjISWN+vBC6V26QiAiExlkat6hdurXDOnCBSel58A4jun+89IdOIxk090ZXmSi1CeYRA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
